## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force has nonlinear dependence on position x, and may include time-dependent driving or damping terms. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by the force law F(x,t)/m.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinearity in restoring force)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric nonlinear oscillator)
- Combined quadratic-cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general polynomial nonlinearity)
- Driven linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * cos(c2 * t) (harmonic driving force)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven cubic oscillator)
- Driven with damping proxy: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (driven Duffing with phase)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2)**(-1) (rational restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force, e.g., pendulum)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order Duffing)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-varying stiffness)
- Nonlinear with periodic drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven pendulum)
- Van der Pol-like: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear damping approximation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-symmetry restoring forces → odd powers of x only (x, x³, x⁵) indicating symmetric potential wells
- Broken symmetry in potential → even powers of x (x²) appear alongside odd powers
- Periodic driving → additive sinusoidal terms in t: cos(c*t) or sin(c*t)
- Parametric excitation → multiplicative coupling x*cos(c*t) indicating time-varying stiffness
- Sinusoidal restoring force sin(c*x) → large-amplitude pendulum-like behavior with bounded potential
- Rational restoring force x/(1+c*x²) → softening spring that saturates at large displacement
- Hardening vs softening spring → sign of cubic coefficient c1 in c0*x + c1*x³ determines stiffening (+) or softening (-)
- Absence of velocity variable with time dependence → driving force or parametric terms must appear explicitly through t

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `-1.15357*x - 1.15357*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.42262*sin(t)`.

The GT has three terms:
1. A linear term in x: `-1.15357*x`
2. A term `x*exp(-|x|)` with coefficient `-1.15357`
3. A sinusoidal term `0.42262*sin(t)`

The key challenge is matching `x*exp(-|x|)`. Note that `exp(-|x|)` is an even function of x, so `x*exp(-|x|)` is an odd function.

Let me check which candidates contain `x*exp(...)` terms that could potentially become `x*exp(-|x|)`:

**Candidates with `x*exp(c*x²)` terms**: 6, 12, 17, 21, 22, 26, 29, 34, 35, 36, 42, 45, 46

For these, `x*exp(c*x²)` with negative c gives `x*exp(-c|x²|) = x*exp(-|c|x²)`, which is NOT the same as `x*exp(-|x|)` since `x²` ≠ `|x|`.

**Candidates with rational functions `x/(cx²+1)`**: These approximate `x*exp(-cx²)` for small x but aren't equivalent to `x*exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidates with `Abs(x)` terms**: These have terms like `x*Abs(x)`, `x³*Abs(x)`, `x⁵*Abs(x)` - polynomial times |x|, not exponential.

**Candidates with `x*cos(c*x)` terms**: 38, 43, 50. Let me check candidate 50:
`c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*cos(c3*t + c4) + c5*x/(c6*x² + 1) + c7*sin(c8*x + c9)`

The term `sin(c8*x + c9)` - this is a sine of x, not `x*exp(-|x|)`.

None of these functional forms can produce `x*exp(-|x|)` exactly.

However, let me reconsider: could any combination of rational functions sum to approximate `x*exp(-|x|)` exactly? No - rational functions and `x*exp(-|x|)` are fundamentally different (rational functions are algebraic, exp is transcendental in a different way).

Wait - I should check if the GT itself might be expressible differently. The Taylor series of `x*exp(-|x|)` involves all powers of |x|, so no finite polynomial/rational combination can match it exactly.

Let me reconsider candidates with `x*exp(c*x²)`. Is `exp(-|x|) = exp(-√(x²))` ever equal to `exp(c*x²)`? No, these are different functions.

Let me look more carefully at candidate 26: `c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*cos(c3*t + c4) + c5*x*exp(c6*x²) + c7*x*Abs(x)`

This has `x*exp(c6*x²)` which gives `x*exp(-a*x²)` (Gaussian decay), not `x*exp(-|x|)`.

And candidate 46: `c0*x + c1*x³ + c2*cos(c3*t + c4) + c5*x/(c6*x² + 1) + c7*x*exp(c8*x²)`

Same issue - `exp(c8*x²)` ≠ `exp(-|x|)`.

None of the candidates contain a term of the form `x*exp(-|x|)` or any functional form that could be made equivalent to it. The candidates use:
- Polynomials in x
- Rational functions of x
- `x*exp(c*x²)` (Gaussian-type)
- `x*|x|`, `x³*|x|` (polynomial × absolute value)
- Trigonometric functions of t and x
- `x*cos(cx)`

None of these can produce `exp(-|x|)` behavior (exponential decay with `|x|`, not `x²`).

Therefore, no candidate can be made equivalent to the GT.
